				<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading pagetitle page-header">
					Les Troyens, H 133 (Berlioz, Hector)				</h1>	

				<div class="body"><div lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="wp_header">
<table>
<table>

<tr>
<th><span class="mh555">Movements/Sections</span><span class="ms555">Mov'ts/Sec's</span>
</th>
<td>5 acts
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Composition Year
</th>
<td>1856–58, with additions 1859–60, 1863 <b>A</b><br />1864 (<i>Marche troyenne</i>) <b>B</b>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Genre Categories<span class="addpagetag mh555"></span>
</th>

<tr>
<th>Misc. Notes
</th>
<td>Bookmarked by Act.<br /><b>Note</b>: The original Act I is here split into “Acts I and II”; the two tableaux of Act II now comprise “Act III”.<br />To accomodate the break in the middle of Act I, the last four bars of page 80 are altered into a final cadence, and the following <i>Hymne troyenne</i> has a new introduction grafted onto the front finishing at figure A on page 82.<br />The <i>Hymne troyenne</i> and <i>Combat de ceste</i> (pp.81–105) are an interpolation of previously typeset score by Choudens <i>ca</i>.1885; the majority of the typesetting appears to be the work of <a href="/wiki/Breitkopf" title="Breitkopf" class="mw-redirect">Breitkopf</a>.
</td></tr>

<th>Copyright
</th>
<td><div class="plainlinks"><a href="/wiki/IMSLP:Public_Domain" title="IMSLP:Public Domain" class="mw-redirect">Public Domain</a><span class="noanon">&#160;<small>[<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://imslp.org/index.php?title=Special:IMSLPMassTagger&amp;indexes=88874/20310">tag</a>/<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://imslp.org/index.php?title=Special:IMSLPMassImageDelete&amp;indexes=88874/20310">del</a>/<span id="fmrglnk" data-pdfstr="88874//20310/"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://imslp.org">mrg</a></span>]</small></span></div>
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th>Misc. Notes
</th>
<td>This reprint of Berlioz’s privately published 1862 vocal score of <i>Les troyens</i> reflects the 1863 performance, which consisted of only half of the opera, and was thus entitled <i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i>. It lacks Acts I and II; it includes the <i>Prélude</i> and a prologue incorporating the <i>Marche troyenne</i>, which were composed to cover the omission of those acts. There are three further cuts in this score, in Acts IV and V: the Act IV duet of Anna and Narbal; the Act V duet of two Trojan soldiers, and the confrontation between Énée and Didon at the end of the same tableau.<br /><b>Note</b>: Act III is renamed as “Act I”; the two tableaux of Act IV become “Acts II and III” respectively; the first tableau of Act V is renamed as “Act IV”, and the remainder of the Act remains as “Act V”. <span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.archive.org/stream/deuximepartied00berl#page/n1">View UNC scan at archive.org</a></span>
</td></tr>
<tr>

<h2> <span class="mw-headline" id="Misc._Comments">Misc. Comments</span></h2>
<p>Conceived as a grand opera in five acts and composed between 1856 and 1858, the work was refused by the Paris Opéra. Berlioz conducted some excerpts at the casino in Baden-Baden, in the Salon de Conversation on 29 August 1859, which included the duets for Cassandre and Chorèbe from Act I, and the duet <i>Nuit d’ivresse</i> for Didon and Énée from Act IV, sung by <a href="/wiki/Category:Viardot,_Pauline" title="Category:Viardot, Pauline">Pauline Viardot</a> and Jules Lefort.
</p><p>The compromises forced upon Berlioz to allow half of the work to be performed in 1863 at the much smaller Théâtre-Lyrique led him to divide the work into two parts, <i>La prise de Troie</i> (The capture of Troy), and <i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i> (The Trojans in Carthage), with a new <i>Prélude à Les Troyens à Carthage</i> composed in 1863 as an overture to the second part, along with a short prologue reworking excerpts from Acts I and II such as the <i>Marche troyenne</i>, which is a recasting of the Act I finale, and subsequently arranged in a concert version early in 1864; the second part was also shorn of the ballet music composed in 1859–60, and the remainder underwent further cuts owing to the difficulties of staging (e.g. the <i>Chasse royale et orage</i>, or Royal Hunt and Storm, was heard only on the opening night).
</p><p><i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i>, was premiéred at the Théâtre-Lyrique, Paris, on 4 November 1863, conducted by <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolphe_Deloffre" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Adolphe Deloffre">Adolphe Deloffre</a>.<br />
<i>La prise de Troie</i> was first performed in concert versions in Paris, by <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jules_Pasdeloup" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Jules Pasdeloup">Pasdeloup</a> at the Cirque d’Hiver and <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89douard_Colonne" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Édouard Colonne">Colonne</a> at the Théâtre du Châtelet on the same day, 7 December 1879, and first staged as an opera in Karlsruhe, Germany, by <a href="/wiki/Category:Mottl,_Felix" title="Category:Mottl, Felix">Felix Mottl</a> on 6 December 1890 (with <i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i> presented on the following night).
</p><p>Performances of the complete opera <i>Les Troyens</i> in five acts as Berlioz intended, did not occur until the 20th century, and the first complete performance in Paris only occurred as lately as <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.hberlioz.com/events/celebrations1.htm#Chatelet">11 October 2003</a> at the Théâtre du Châtelet.
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h4> <span class="mw-headline" id="Publication_History">Publication History</span></h4>
<ul><li> 1862: Publication of complete Piano-Vocal Score by means of private subscription by Berlioz through the printer Thierry. Five copies and 3 proof copies extant.
</li><li> 1863: As Léon Carvalho was unable to stage the entire opera, Berlioz modified it to allow it to be staged as two operas; thus <a href="/wiki/Choudens" title="Choudens">Antoine Choudens</a> reprinted the 1862 publication in two volumes, A.C. 987 (<i>La Prise de Troie</i>) and A.C. 988 (<i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i>), adding to the latter the newly composed material for the 1863 performance. Both went on sale but as the run of performances had increasing numbers of cuts made, Choudens similarly trimmed the latter Vocal Score to match. Later reissued after 1889 in one volume.
</li><li> 1885: Choudens published full score of <i>Les Troyens à Carthage</i> (plate A.C 6030).
</li><li> 1892: Choudens printed a new edition of the vocal scores, incorporating a new piano reduction by Louis Narici: A.C. 11,258 (<i>Les Troyens</i> [<i>à Carthage</i>]) and A.C. 11,312 (<i>La Prise de Troie</i>), the latter score may have been released somewhat later (the Variations project copy includes a list of artists involved in Taffanel’s 1899 performance).
</li><li> 1899: Choudens issued a full score of <i>La Prise de Troie</i> to coincide with a performance staged in Paris on 15 November 1899. (plate A.C. 11,222)
</li><li> Leipzig: <a href="/wiki/Breitkopf_%26_H%C3%A4rtel" title="Breitkopf &amp; Härtel" class="mw-redirect">Breitkopf &amp; Härtel</a>, n.d., as part of <a href="/wiki/Hector_Berlioz:_Hector_Berlioz_Werke" title="Hector Berlioz: Hector Berlioz Werke" class="mw-redirect">Hector Berlioz Werke</a> (1900–07), Supplement, Band XXII–XXIII, edited by Charles Malherbe and Felix Weingartner. Apparently a reprint of the Choudens full score with minimal editorial reworking; reprinted in the Kalmus Miniature Score series.
</li><li> Kassel: <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A4renreiter" title="Bärenreiter">Bärenreiter</a>, 1969–70, BA 5442/I–III, as part of <a href="/wiki/Hector_Berlioz:_New_Berlioz_Edition" title="Hector Berlioz: New Berlioz Edition" class="mw-redirect">New Berlioz Edition</a> (1967–2005), Volume 2a (Acts I, II), 2b (Acts III–V), 2c (Supplement), edited by Hugh Macdonald. First complete full score.
</li></ul>
<dl><dd>Vocal score, BA 5442a, with German translation by Simon Werle, and piano reduction by Eike Wernhard after Berlioz’s vocal score.
</dd></dl>
<p><br />
</p>
